الفعل الممكن بالذات وفي العادة احترز به عن المحال بالذات فإن تكليفه غير صحيح والعادي إذ التكليف به غير واقع الذي تمت شرائط وجوبه احترز به عما لم تتم شرائط وجوبه إذ ظاهر أنه لا يصح وجوبه وتكليفه به عند أحد إذا علم الآمر انتفاء شرط وقوعه المكلف من احترز به عما جهل شرط وقوعه وزاد قوله عند وقته تنبيها على أن المعتبر في انتفاء الشرط ذلك الوقت أما لو عدم وقت التكليف ووجد في ذلك الوقت يصح به التكليف البتة هل يصح التكليف به قال الجمهور يصح التكليف به بل يقع خلافا للمعتزلة والإمام في الحاشية قال السبكي الشرائط منها ما يتبادر الذهن إليه وقت سماع التكليف كالعلم والحياة وهذا هو الذي يخالف فيه الإمام ومنها ما لا يتبادر كانتفاء الإرادة لإيمان أبي جهل وهذا لا خلاف فيه اه فعلى هذا لا خلاف في المعنى فإنه ظاهر أن الحياة والعلم من شرائط الوجوب وكذا التمييز وأما شرائط الوقوع فالفرق بالتبادر وعدمه لا معنى له وفي صورة الجهل من الآمر يصح التكليف اتفاقا لا يقال كما قال في التحرير قد تقدم في مسألة امتناع التكليف بالمحال أن الإجماع منعقد على صحة التكليف بما علم الله تعالى أنه يقع ومعلوم أن كل ما لا يقع فبانتفاء شرط من شروطه من إرادة قديمة كما هو رأينا أو حادثة كما هو رأي المعتزلة فقد اتحد ما علم الله أنه لا يقع في الوقت وما علم الله أنه ينتفي شرط من شروطه فحكاية الخلاف ها هنا مناقضة لما نقلوا هناك من الاتفاق لأنا نقول الإجماع كان بالنظر إلى الإمكان الذاتي والصحة دون الوقوع كما يدل عليه كلام بعض المحققين في شرح المختصر عند نقل الإجماع حيث قال الإجماع منعقد على صحة التكليف بما علم الله أنه لا يقع وإن ظن قوم أنه ممتنع لغيره فالخلاف ها هنا في الوقوع للتكليف بما علم الله انتفاء شرط من شروطه بعد الاتفاق على الصحة صحة ذاتية واعلم أن في كلام ابن الحاجب ها هنا أيضا وقع لفظ الصحة فالمناقضة لازمة عليه نعم إرادة الوقوع من الصحة لدفع المناقضة غير بعيد لكن دليل المخالفين يأبى عن هذه الإرادة وقد قال في شرح الشرح عند نقل الإجماع بل على تحققه والظاهر في كلام شارح المختصر أن ضمير أنه يرجع إلى ما علم الله يعني وإن كان قوم ظنوا أن ما علم الله عدمه ممتنع بالغير لكن على صحة التكليف به انعقد الإجماع ثم إنه لا يصح خلاف أحد ممن يدعي التدين فضلا عن مثل إمام الحرمين الذي له يد طولى في العلوم الشرعية كيف ويلزم أن يكون الكافر المص الذي مات على كفره غير مكلف كأبي جهل وكذا العاصي وتنتفي فائدة تبليغ الرسل إلى المصرين لعدم كونهم مكلفين بل يصير تعرضهم وقتلهم ظلما لعدم كونهم عاصين في كفرهم تاركين للمأمور به مرتكبين للمنهي عنه وأي شناعة فوق هذه الشناعات فالحق أنه لا خلاف فيه هذا لنا لو لم يصح التكليف بما علم انتفاء شرطه لم يعلم أحد أنه مكلف قبل وقت الفعل لجواز أن لا يوجد شرط من شروطه جوازا مشعورا للمكلف والتالي باطل وكذا المقدم وقد أنكر قوم العلم بالتكليف قبله فمنعوا بطلان اللازم وذلك الإنكار باطل للإجماع على تحقق الوجوب قبل التمكن بل على تحقق العلم بالوجوب والإجماع نقله القاضي وربما يمنع ولذا زاد قوله بدليل وجوب الشروع بنية أداء الواجب إجماعا وهو فرع تحقق الوجوب بل علمه وربما يمنع الإجماع على وجوب النية بأداء الواجب فإن الحنفية يجوزون أداء الصوم بإطلاق النية ونية النفل فإن قلت لعل الإجماع كان قبل الحنفية والشافعية قلت لو كان قبل لعرفوه لأنهم أصحاب فحص عظيم وأما بعدهم فلا إجماع إلا بدخولهم فالحق في الجواب أن في الواجب الموسع والعمري إجماعا بلا ريب وهذا القدر يكفينا في المطلوب ثم ربما يورد إن أريد بالعلم الجزم فلا يتحقق قبل الوقوع لاحتمال الموت قبله وإن أريد الظن القوي فلا نسلم امتناعه إذ ظن وجود الشرط ممكن وهذا أيضا غير واف لأن في أكثر الأوقات لا يتيسر الظن الضعيف فضلا عن القوي المعتزلة قالوا أولا عدم شرطه غير ممكن لأن وجود المشروط بدون الشرط محال والإمكان شرط التكليف فانتفى شرطه فانتفى التكليف وهذا الاستدلال يرشدك أيضا إلى أن المقصود في هذه المسألة الصحة العقلية لا الوقوعية قلنا إن أردتم أن ما عدم شرطه غير ممكن بالذات فممنوع فإن الضرورة قاضية بأن الامتثال من أبي جهل ممكن بالإمكانين وإن أردتم أنه غير ممكن بسبب عدم الشرط فمسلم لكن لا ينافي الإمكان ذاتا وعادة والشرط للتكليف الإمكان العادي الأخص من الذاتي وهو لا ينافي الامتناع لغيره وقلنا أيضا منقوض بجهل الآمر بعد الشرط في الواقع لأن المعدوم الشرط في الواقع المجهول عند الآمر غير ممكن في الواقع إذ لا دخل للعلم في الإمكان والامتناع فإنه أي العلم بالإمكان والامتناع تابع للمعلوم لا أنه سبب كيف والإمكان لا يكون من الغير فإذا كان ممتنعا فقد فات شرط التكليف فلا التكليف به أيضا وفيه أن التكليف يصح بالمحال عند الجهل بالاستحالة وقد مر الإشارة إليه لكن لا يصح أن يكون المحال مكلفا به في الواقع إذ صحة الإيقاع من ضروريات كونه مطلوبا فتدبر وقالوا ثانيا لو صح التكليف مع علم الآمر بانتفاء شرطه لصح مع علم المأمور بانتفائه لأن عدم الحصول مشترك ولا يتخيل المانع إلا هو ولم يبق على زعمكم واللازم باطل اتفاقا إذ لا يصح مع علم المأمور قلنا أولا بطلان اللازم ممنوع فإنه قد مر أن الإنسان لم يترك سدى وقلنا ثانيا تنزلا لم يكن عدم صحة التكليف هناك لعدم الحصول بل لانتفاء الفائدة من التكليف وهو الابتلاء ويرد عليه أنه يتحقق الابتلاء فإن عزم على الفعل وبكى لانعدام شرطه استحق الثواب وإلا لا هذا فالحق أن علم المأمور بعدم الوقوع غير مانع من التكليف كما قد مر من المصنف
The act possible in essence and custom: He guarded against the impossible in essence, for its obligation is not valid, and [against] the customary [impossible], for obligation of it is not actual. [The act] for which the conditions of its obligation are complete: He guarded against that for which the conditions of its obligation are not complete, for it is apparent that its obligation and obligation upon it are not valid according to anyone if the commander knows the non-existence of a condition of its occurrence. The obligated person: He guarded against one who is ignorant of the condition of its occurrence. And he added his statement 'at its time' as a reminder that the consideration in the non-existence of the condition is that time. As for if it is absent at the time of obligation and present at that time, obligation upon it is definitely valid. Is obligation upon it valid? The majority said: obligation upon it is valid, rather it occurs, contrary to the Mu'tazila and Imam [al-Haramayn] in the Hashiya. Al-Subki said: The conditions include that which immediately comes to mind at the time of hearing the obligation, like knowledge and life, and this is what the Imam disagrees upon. And [conditions] include that which does not come to mind, like the non-existence of will for the faith of Abu Jahl, and there is no disagreement on this. So according to this, there is no disagreement in meaning, for it is apparent that life and knowledge are from the conditions of obligation, as is discernment. As for the conditions of occurrence, the difference by immediacy and non-immediacy has no meaning. In the case of ignorance of the commander, the obligation is valid by agreement. It cannot be said, as said in al-Tahrir, that it was already presented in the issue of the impossibility of obligation upon the impossible that consensus is established upon the validity of obligation upon what Allah knows will occur, and it is known that everything that does not occur is due to the non-existence of a condition of its conditions from an eternal will as is our view or an originated will as is the view of the Mu'tazila. So what Allah knows will not occur at the time and what Allah knows will have a condition of its conditions non-existent have become one. So relating the disagreement here is contradictory to what they transmitted there of agreement. Because we say: The consensus was with consideration to essential possibility and validity, not occurrence, as indicated by the statement of some verifiers in Sharh al-Mukhtasar when transmitting consensus, where he said: Consensus is established upon the validity of obligation upon what Allah knows will not occur, even if some people thought it is impossible due to another. So the disagreement here is about occurrence of obligation upon what Allah knows that a condition of its conditions is non-existent, after agreement on validity—essential validity. And know that in the statement of Ibn al-Hajib here also the word validity occurred, so the contradiction is necessary upon him. Yes, intending occurrence from validity to repel the contradiction is not far, but the evidence of the opponents refuses this intention. And he said in Sharh al-Sharh when transmitting consensus: rather upon its actuality, and the apparent in the statement of the commentator of al-Mukhtasar is that the pronoun 'it' refers to what Allah knows, meaning even if some people thought that what Allah knows is non-existent is impossible due to another, but upon the validity of obligation upon it consensus is established. Then the disagreement of anyone who claims religiosity is not valid, let alone someone like Imam al-Haramayn who has great mastery in the religious sciences. How? It would necessitate that the persistent disbeliever who died upon his disbelief is not obligated like Abu Jahl, and likewise the sinner, and the benefit of sending messengers to the persistent would be negated due to them not being obligated, rather their exposure and killing would be oppression due to them not being disobedient in their disbelief, leaving the commanded and committing the prohibited. And what disgrace is beyond these disgraces? So the truth is that there is no disagreement in this. This is for us. If obligation upon what is known that its condition is non-existent were not valid, then no one would know that he is obligated before the time of the act due to the possibility that a condition of its conditions does not exist—a possibility perceived by the obligated—and the consequent is false, and likewise the antecedent. And some people denied knowledge of obligation before it, so they prevented the falsehood of the necessary. And that denial is false due to consensus upon the actuality of obligation before capability, rather upon the actuality of knowledge of obligation, and the consensus is transmitted by al-Qadi, and perhaps it is denied, and therefore he added his statement: 'By the evidence of the obligation of beginning with the intention of performing the obligatory by consensus, and it is a branch of the actuality of obligation, rather its knowledge.' And perhaps consensus on the obligation of intention for performing the obligatory is denied, for the Hanafis permit performing the fast with absolute intention and intention of supererogatory. If you say: Perhaps the consensus was before the Hanafis and Shafi'is. I say: If it was before, they would have known it because they are great investigators. As for after them, there is no consensus except by their inclusion. So the truth in the answer is that in the expanded obligatory and the life-long obligatory there is consensus without doubt, and this amount suffices us in what is required. Then perhaps it is objected: If by knowledge is meant certainty, it is not actualized before occurrence due to the possibility of death before it. And if by it is meant strong conjecture, then we do not concede its impossibility, for conjecture of the existence of the condition is possible. This also is not sufficient because in most times weak conjecture is not available, let alone strong. The Mu'tazila said firstly: The non-existence of its condition is not possible because the existence of the conditioned without the condition is impossible, and possibility is a condition of the obligation. So its condition is non-existent, so the obligation is non-existent. And this reasoning also guides you to the fact that the intended in this issue is rational validity, not occurrential validity. We said: If you mean that what has its condition non-existent is impossible in essence, then it is denied, for necessity judges that compliance from Abu Jahl is possible in both possibilities. And if you mean that it is impossible due to the non-existence of the condition, then it is conceded, but it does not negate possibility in essence and custom, and the condition for obligation is customary possibility, which is more specific than essential possibility, and it does not negate impossibility due to another. And we also said: It is invalidated by the commander's ignorance of the condition in reality, because what has its condition non-existent in reality when unknown to the commander is impossible in reality, for knowledge has no role in possibility and impossibility—rather knowledge of possibility and impossibility follows the known, it is not a cause. How? And possibility is not from another. So if it is impossible, then the condition of obligation is missing, so there is no obligation upon it either. And in this, obligation upon the impossible is valid when ignorant of the impossibility, as has been indicated, but it is not correct that the impossible be obligated upon in reality, for the validity of occurrence is among the necessities of it being required. So ponder. And they said secondly: If obligation with the commander's knowledge of the non-existence of its condition is valid, then it would be valid with the knowledge of the obligated person of its non-existence, because the non-concurrence is shared, and no other obstacle can be imagined except that, and it remains not according to your claim, and the necessary is false by agreement, because it is not valid with the knowledge of the obligated person. We said firstly: The falsehood of the necessary is denied, for it has passed that man is not left in vain. And we said secondly by way of assumption: The non-validity of obligation there was not due to non-concurrence but due to the non-existence of the benefit of obligation, which is trial. It is responded that trial is actualized, for if he resolves to do the act and weeps due to the non-existence of its condition, he deserves reward, otherwise not. This is it. So the truth is that the obligated person's knowledge of non-occurrence does not prevent obligation, as has passed from the author.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh regarding the validity of taklif (obligation) when Allah knows that a necessary condition for the act's occurrence will not be met. The majority (including the Hanafis) hold that such taklif is valid, contrary to the Mu'tazila and Imam al-Haramayn. The author first defines the subject: the act must be possible in essence and custom, excluding the intrinsically impossible and the customarily impossible (like flying without means). He further distinguishes between conditions of obligation (e.g., life, knowledge, discernment) and conditions of occurrence (e.g., will, ability). The dispute centers on whether the commander's knowledge of the absence of a condition for occurrence invalidates the obligation. The Hanafi position is that taklif is based on intrinsic and customary possibility, not on actual occurrence. Even if Allah knows the condition will be absent, the act remains possible in essence and custom, so taklif is valid. This is supported by consensus on the validity of taklif for what Allah knows will not occur, such as the obligations upon Abu Jahl. The author refutes objections from the Mu'tazila, who argue that the missing condition makes the act impossible and thus taklif invalid. The Hanafi response is that the impossibility is extrinsic (due to the missing condition), not intrinsic, and the required possibility for taklif is intrinsic and customary, which can coexist with extrinsic impossibility. The passage also addresses the issue of the obligated person's knowledge of the missing condition, concluding that even that does not prevent valid taklif, as the benefit (trial) is still possible.

Key Terms
التكليف (al-taklif): The imposition of a legal obligation upon a person (mukallaf).
الإمكان الذاتي (al-imkan al-dhati): Intrinsic possibility: the act is possible in its essence, not requiring any external condition.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition, without which the act cannot occur (shart al-wuju') or the obligation cannot be valid (shart al-wujub).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, why is taklif valid even when Allah knows a condition for the act's occurrence will not be met?
A) Because the act is possible in essence and custom, and extrinsic impossibility does not negate that.
B) Because Allah's knowledge does not affect the act's reality.
C) Because the Mu'tazila agree on this point.
D) Because the condition is irrelevant for taklif.

Key Takeaway
Taklif is valid despite Allah's knowledge of a missing condition because the required possibility is intrinsic and customary, not dependent on actual occurrence; the benefit of trial remains.

Validity of a Discerning Child's Islam
Stating that the Islam of a discerning child is valid with evidence and an objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the dalil used in Hanafi usul for the validity of a child's Islam and analyze a methodological objection to that dalil.

Core Idea
The Prophet's acceptance of 'Ali's childhood Islam proves that a discerning child's faith is legally effective.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut, a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut, presents the Hanafi ruling that the Islam of a discerning child (al-sabi al-aqil) is valid. The proof is the well-known case of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib accepting Islam as a child, which the Prophet accepted. The text then raises an objection challenging whether this evidence truly supports the ruling. Let's examine the proof and the critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Subject
Locate the central ruling: 'yasu Islam al-sabi al-aqil sahih' (the Islam of a discerning child is valid). The subject is a child who has reached the age of tamyiz (discernment), around 7 years old.
The ruling is about validity (sihha), not obligation. The child's act of becoming Muslim is legally effective.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites the Prophet's acceptance of 'Ali's Islam when 'Ali was seven (or eight or ten) years old. This is a narrated action (Sunnah ahad).
The dalil is a specific historical incident, not a general command.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The wajh (indication) is that the Prophet's acceptance demonstrates that the child's Islam is valid and carries legal effects. If it were not valid, the Prophet would not have accepted it.
The Hanafi position relies on the Qur'anic principle of accepting the Prophet's actions as evidence.
4
Identify the Objection
The text presents an objection: this incident does not prove the required point because the dispute is about the validity of the child's faith in terms of rulings (ahkam), not about the mere act of acceptance.
The objector argues that the dalil is insufficient to establish that the child's Islam is valid for all purposes (e.g., inheritance, burial). The full response is missing from the text.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Response (Hypothetical)
Based on Hanafi usul, the response would likely argue that the Prophet's acceptance implies full legal validity unless there is evidence to the contrary. The child's Islam is effective immediately, as there is no condition of puberty for validity.
This step is reconstructed because the original text is incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصح إسلام الصبي العاقل صحيح بدليل صحة إسلام أمير المؤمنين علي رضي الله عنه أو ثمان أو عشر سنين والكل أحوال الصبا وقبل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنه كان آمن وهو ابن سبع واعترض عليه بأنه لا يدل على المطلوب فإن النزاع إنما هو في صحة إيمانه في حق أحكام
The Islam of a discerning child is valid, by the evidence of the validity of the Islam of the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, at eight or ten years, and all are states of childhood, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, accepted it, for he (Ali) had faith while he was seven. And it is objected that this does not indicate the required point, because the dispute is about the validity of his faith in terms of rulings...
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that the Islam of a discerning child (al-sabi al-aqil) is valid. The evidence is the case of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra), who accepted Islam as a child (at age 7, 8, or 10) and the Prophet (saw) accepted his Islam. The passage notes an objection that this only proves acceptance in the sense of future rulings (ahkam), not that the contract itself was valid at that time. However, the Hanafi position is that the child's Islam is valid for all purposes, based on this and other evidences.

Key Terms
الصبي العاقل (al-sabi al-aqil): A child who has reached the age of discernment (tamyiz), typically around 7 years old.
صحة إسلامه (sihhat islamihi): The validity of the child's Islam, meaning it is effective in terms of rulings (ahkam) such as inheritance, burial, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence is cited in this passage to support the validity of a child's Islam?
A) The Prophet's acceptance of 'Ali's Islam when 'Ali was seven years old.
B) The consensus of the Companions.
C) A verse from the Quran.
D) The practice of the first four caliphs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a discerning child's Islam based on the Prophet's acceptance of 'Ali's childhood conversion.

Conditions for Taklif: Intellect and Puberty
Establishing 'aql and bulugh as conditions for taklif with disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the conditions for legal obligation (taklif), identify the primary dalil (the hadith of the lifted pen), and explain the disagreements with other schools.

Core Idea
Taklif requires sanity and puberty—a child is not obligated, but his actions have legal consequences.

In this lesson, we explore a foundational rule of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: what conditions must be met for a person to be held accountable for religious obligations? The passage establishes that intellect ('aql) is a condition, but it is attached to the criterion of puberty (bulugh) as a plausible locus for complete intellect. The primary evidence is the well-known hadith 'the pen is lifted from three persons.' We will also examine and respond to alternative views from al-Maturidi, the Mu'tazila, and Qadi Abu Zaid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its rationale
The passage states that intellect is a condition for taklif, defined as the instrument of understanding. However, taklif is not attached to every degree of intellect; rather, it is attached to a moderate degree, which is found in the sane adult. Puberty (bulugh) is the marker because it is a plausible locus for perfection of intellect.
Note that even if an adult's intellect is less than some adolescents, the ruling is still attached to puberty due to hardship (mashaqqa).
2
Locate the primary dalil and its application
The hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاثة' (the pen is lifted from three) is the main evidence. It explicitly excludes the sleeping, the child, and the insane from accountability (mua'akhadha). The Hanafi school uses this to argue that no obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') is upon the pre-pubescent child.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but widely accepted; its indication (dalala) is qat'i regarding non-accountability.
3
Analyze the disagreements
Three opposing views are presented: (1) Abu Mansur al-Maturidi holds that a sane child is obligated specifically for iman due to intellect and hadiths about children of disbelievers. (2) The Mu'tazila hold that the child is punished for abandoning iman. (3) Qadi Abu Zaid holds that all rights of Allah (including iman and other acts) are obligatory but performance drops due to physical deficiency.
The Hanafi response is that the hadith is general and applies to all children regardless of sanity; the presentation of Islam to a child is for validity, not obligation. Striking at ten for prayer is disciplinary, not for obligation.
4
Examine the Hanafi secondary evidence
The passage provides a second piece of evidence: the case of a girl nearing puberty (murahiqa). According to Imam Muhammad, if she does not describe faith when asked, her marriage is not annulled, unlike an adult woman. This shows she is not commanded to have faith. However, the commentator notes that explicit disbelief annuls the marriage, indicating she is prohibited from kufr.
This evidence is a statement of a mujtahid (Imam Muhammad) and not a direct revelation, but it reflects the school's position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical consequence of this disagreement is that in the Hanafi school, a child cannot be held sinful for not performing prayers or not professing faith before puberty. However, his conversion is valid and carries legal effects (e.g., his marriage to a believer remains valid, and he inherits as a Muslim). The child is also obligated to refrain from explicit disbelief.
This distinction avoids both holding children accountable inappropriately and ignoring their legal capacity for valid actions.

Source Text

Issue: The opening of al-Rahmut sharh Musallam al-Thubut, volume one. 'Intellect is a condition for legal obligation (taklif). Then it has interpretations, the most apparent of which is that it is the instrument of understanding. Elaborating on the rest does not avoid tedious prolixity since understanding occurs through it and not through anything else, and it varies in strength and weakness. (And taklif is not attached to every degree of intellects; rather, the mercy of God required that it be attached to a moderate degree. So it is attached to being an adult who is sane (i.e., not insane) because it is a plausible locus for the perfection of intellect. So taklif revolves around it (existence and non-existence), not around the perfection or deficiency of intellect. For among adults are those whose intellect is deficient compared to some adolescents, such as a traveler. The ruling is attached to it because it is a plausible locus of hardship, and hardship is something not precisely defined. So the ruling revolves around it (existence and non-existence), whether hardship is found or not. Al-Bayhaqi (the muhaddith, may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'The legal rulings were attached to puberty after the Hijrah; before that, up to the year of Khandaq, they were attached to discernment (tamyiz).' This supports the attachment of rulings to puberty. And if their attachment to puberty is established, then (no obligation of performance is due upon a child (sabi)) even if he is sane, (contrary to Abu Mansur). And this is the Imam, the scholar, 'Alam al-Huda al-Maturidi, the greatest of our scholars and the greatest of the scholars of Iraq. Likewise in al-Taqrir and al-Hashiyah. (And) contrary to the Mu'tazila regarding the obligation of faith (i.e., the obligation of its performance), for they held that he is punished for abandoning it. (And) contrary to al-Qadi Abu Zaid, who said that all the rights of Allah (including faith and other acts) are obligatory upon him, except that performance drops due to the excuse of childhood due to physical deficiency. Perhaps he only said the dropping regarding other than faith. For us, firstly: his saying, peace be upon him: 'The pen is lifted' (i.e., of reckoning and punishment) from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' The followers of Imam 'Alam al-Huda specifically exclude the sane child regarding the obligation of faith due to intellect and due to the hadiths about the children of disbelievers entering the Fire. If you say: Why then is Islam presented to the child after the conversion of his wife, and it is not obligatory upon him? Likewise, he is not commanded to perform the prayer when he is ten years old. He answered the first: 'The presentation of Islam to him after the conversion of his wife is for its validity, not for its obligation.' If you say: Since the child is not obligated (mukallaf), the address regarding the prohibition of marriage with a disbeliever does not apply to him. So where does the invalidity of the marriage come from such that presentation is needed? Rather, there must be a proof. I say: We have explained that the causality of faith for the termination of guardianship from a disbeliever is textual in numerous texts, and it necessitates the invalidity of the marriage and the non-establishment of inheritance and other things. He answered the second: 'Striking [the boy] at ten for prayer is disciplinary, i.e., striking for discipline, not for punishment. For habituation, not for obligation. i.e., striking so they get used to it, not because they are obligated.' (And) for us, secondly: the non-annulment of the marriage of a girl nearing puberty (murahiqa) due to her lack of description [of faith]. Imam Muhammad said: 'If a girl nearing puberty does not describe faith when asked about it, her marriage is not annulled, contrary to the adult woman, for her marriage is annulled.' So it is known that the girl nearing puberty was not commanded to have faith. And it is not hidden from the alert that this is not suitable as a proof, for it is the statement of a mujtahid, not the statement of the Lawgiver. Then there is distortion of words from their places. For our scholars, such as Imam Fakhr al-Islam and others, argued that the school of our imams is that, and the evidence indicates it. Then it has been established that the marriage of a girl nearing puberty is annulled by explicit disbelief, so it is known that she is explicitly prohibited from disbelief. And some commentators on the Usul of Imam Fakhr al-Islam explicitly stated that disbelief is forbidden for a child, obligated to refrain, and on this basis, he should be disobedient in the case of not describing [faith], and the marriage is annulled. And he is...
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a rule (usul rule) establishing that intellect ('aql) is a condition for legal obligation (taklif), and that the criterion for obligation is puberty (bulugh) combined with sanity. The commentator explains that 'aql is the instrument of understanding and varies among individuals. Taklif is not attached to every degree of intellect but to a moderate degree, which is found in the sane adult. Puberty is considered a plausible locus for perfection of intellect. Even if an adult's intellect is less than some adolescents, the ruling is still attached to puberty because it is a plausible locus of hardship, and hardship is not precisely defined. Al-Bayhaqi's statement supports that before the Hijrah, rulings were based on discernment (tamyiz), but after Hijrah and especially after the Battle of Khandaq, they were based on puberty. The passage then discusses disagreements: Abu Mansur al-Maturidi held that a sane child is obligated (specifically for iman), the Mu'tazila held that the child is punished for abandoning iman, and Qadi Abu Zaid held that all of Allah's rights are obligatory on the child but performance drops due to childhood. The Hanafi position, supported by the hadith 'the pen is lifted,' is that no obligation of performance is upon a child. The commentator addresses an objection: why is Islam presented to a child after his spouse converts? Answer: for validity, not obligation. The hadith about striking at ten for prayer is disciplinary, not obligatory. Then a second evidence is given: the marriage of a girl nearing puberty (murahiqa) is not annulled if she does not describe faith, unlike an adult, proving she is not commanded. However, the commentator notes this is a weak proof because it is a statement of a mujtahid, not the Lawgiver. Later, he clarifies that explicit disbelief does annul the marriage of a murahiqa, proving she is prohibited from disbelief. The passage ends with the view that a child is obligated to refrain from disbelief.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): The instrument of understanding (alat al-fahm), which varies in strength and weakness among individuals. It is a condition (shart) for taklif.
البلوغ (al-bulugh): Puberty, which is the criterion (mazinnah) for the perfection of intellect and the attachment of legal rulings. It is the marker for taklif existence.
التمييز (al-tamyiz): Discernment, the ability to distinguish between good and bad, which was the basis for legal rulings before the Hijrah up to the Battle of Khandaq, according to al-Bayhaqi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It results in the annulment of the child's marriage, like an adult.
B) It does not annul the child's marriage because the child is not commanded to have faith.
C) It is considered a sin because the child is obligated to profess faith.
D) It is irrelevant because a child cannot have a valid marriage.

Key Takeaway
A child is not obligated to perform acts of worship, but his valid acts carry reward and his conversion has legal effects.

Legal Capacity (Ahlīyah): Definition, Types, and Effects on Children's Acts
Defining ahlīyah and classifying its two types with implications for taklif.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ahlīyah, distinguish complete from deficient capacity, and state the ruling (valid vs obligatory) for a child's purely beneficial acts.

Core Idea
Complete capacity obliges performance; deficient capacity allows validity but not obligation.

This passage from Fawātih al-Rahamūt defines the foundational usul concept of ahlīyah (legal capacity) and divides it into complete and deficient. Understanding this distinction is critical because it determines whether an action is obligatory or merely valid. The author then applies this framework to a concrete case: the legal effect of a rational child's acts, particularly faith (īmān).

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of ahlīyah
Ahlīyah is the eligibility of a human being for a ruling to be attached. It comes in two forms: complete (kāmilah) and deficient (qāsirah).
The definition is: 'كون الإنسان بحيث يصح أن يتعلق به الحكم'.
2
Identify the two types and their causes
Complete capacity requires perfection of both intellect (ʿaql) and body (badan) – being an adult sane person (bāligh ʿāqil). Deficient capacity results from deficiency in either, e.g., a rational child (body deficient) or an adult imbecile (intellect deficient).
The passage explicitly mentions these examples.
3
Note the legal effect of each type
Complete capacity entails obligation of performance (wujūb al-adā'). Deficient capacity only establishes validity of performance (sihhat al-adā'), not obligation.
This is the core ruling: obligation vs mere validity.
4
Classify actions into rights of God and rights of the servant
Actions are divided into huqūq Allāh (rights of God) and huqūq al-ʿabd (rights of the servant). Each is further subdivided into three categories: pure good, pure evil, and intermediate; and purely beneficial, purely harmful, and intermediate respectively.
This classification helps determine which acts are valid from one with deficient capacity.
5
Apply to the example of faith (īmān) by a rational child
Faith is pure good and purely beneficial; therefore, it is valid from a child by qiyas and istihsan. Objections based on apparent harms (like loss of inheritance) are refuted because the harm stems from the disbelief of the relative, not from faith itself.
The passage provides a detailed argument for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة عن (الأهلية) هي كون الإنسان بحيث يصح أن يتعلق به الحكم كاملة بكمال العقل والبدن) أي كونه عاقلاً بالغاً (فيلزم وجوب الأداء وقاصرة بقصور أحدهما كالصبي العاقل) فإن بدنه قاصر والمعتوه البالغ) لقصور عقله والثابت معها أي القاصرة صحة الأداء) لا وجوبه كما قد مر (والتفصيل في الصبي) ويقاس عليه المعتوه أن ما يكون مع القاصرة إما حق الله) ما وهو روعي فيه جانب الشرع (وهو ثلاثة حسن محض) أي الذي لا يمكن سقوط حسنه بحال (وقبيح (محض) أي لا يمكن أن يسقط قبحه بحال (وبين) بين أي أمر قد يحسن وقد يقبح (وإما حق العبد) وهو الذي روعي فيه مصالح العبد في تشريعه (وهو أيضاً ثلاثة : نافع محض) في الدنيا وضار محض فيها ودائر بينهما) قد ينفع وقد يضر الأول) (كالإيمان) فإنه حسن محض (لا يسقط حسنه وفيه نفع محض، لأنه مناط سعادة الدارين أما السعادة الأخروية فظاهرة، وأما سعادة الدنيا فلأنه يصير بالإيمان معصوم الدم والمال ومعززاً بين الأنام، وإذا كان نافعاً محضاً (فيصح منه) قياساً واستحساناً، لأنه محل الرحمة، فيصح ما فيه نفعه، وإن قيل: لعلّ الشرع لم يعتبره وجعله كلا إيمان قال : ( والحجر من الشارع لم يوجد ولا يليق به) فإن الحكيم لا يليق به أن يحجر عما مناط السعادتين، فإن قلت فيه ضرر أيضاً من حرمان الميراث إذا كان المورث كافراً، وفرقة النكاح إذا كانت الزوجة كافرة، أجاب بقوله: (وضرر حرمان الميراث وفرقة النكاح ليس مبنياً على الإيمان، بل لكفر القريب والزوجة) فإن كفرهما مع
Question: About legal capacity (ahlīyah): it is the state of the human being such that it is valid for a ruling to be attached to him. Complete capacity is with perfection of intellect and body, i.e., being an adult sane person, so obligation of performance applies. Deficient capacity is with deficiency of either, like the rational child, for his body is deficient, and the adult imbecile (ma'tuh), for deficiency of intellect. What is established with it, i.e., deficient capacity, is validity of performance, not its obligation, as has passed. And the detail of the child (and the imbecile is analogized to him) is: what is with deficient capacity is either a right of God (which considers the aspect of law) and it is three: pure good (whose goodness cannot fall away in any case), pure evil (whose evil cannot fall away in any case), and intermediate (something that may be good or evil); or a right of the slave (which considers the interests of the slave in its legislation) and it is also three: purely beneficial in this world, purely harmful in it, and between the two (may benefit or harm). The first (pure good) is like faith: it is pure good, its goodness does not fall away, and it contains pure benefit because it is the locus of happiness in both abodes. As for otherworldly happiness, it is apparent. As for worldly happiness, because by faith one becomes inviolable in blood and property and honored among people. And when it is purely beneficial, it is valid from him (the child) by analogy (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan), because he is a locus of mercy, so what benefits him is valid. If it is said: Perhaps the Lawgiver did not consider it and made it like 'no faith', he said: 'Guardianship (hajr) from the Lawgiver does not exist, nor is it befitting to Him', for the Wise is not befitting to put guardianship over that which is the locus of the two happinesses. If you say: There is also harm in it from deprivation of inheritance if the testator is a disbeliever, and separation of marriage if the wife is a disbeliever. He answered: 'The harm of deprivation of inheritance and separation of marriage is not based on faith, but on the disbelief of the relative and wife.' For their disbelief with...
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is an usul definition of legal capacity (ahlīyah) and its classifications. The author defines ahlīyah as the eligibility of a person for a ruling to be attached. Complete capacity requires both perfect intellect (ʿaql) and physical maturity (bulūgh); with it, obligation of performance (wujūb al-adā') is inherent. Deficient capacity occurs when either intellect or body is deficient, as in a rational child (body deficient) or an adult imbecile (intellect deficient). With deficient capacity, only validity of performance (sihhat al-adā') is established, not obligation. The author then classifies actions that can be performed by one with deficient capacity. They are divided into two categories: rights of God (huqūq Allāh) and rights of the servant (huqūq al-ʿabd). Rights of God are further divided into three: purely good (like faith), purely evil (like disbelief), and intermediate (like some transactional acts). Rights of the servant are similarly three: purely beneficial, purely harmful, and intermediate. For the child (and analogously the imbecile), actions that are purely good and purely beneficial (like faith) are valid from him—by qiyas and istihsan—because he is a locus of mercy, so acts that bring benefit are considered valid. The author refutes potential objections: the Lawgiver would not impose guardianship (hajr) over something that is the source of both worldly and otherworldly happiness. Regarding the apparent harm from faith (like loss of inheritance or marriage), this harm is attributed to the disbelief of the relative, not to faith itself. The passage establishes that while a child is not obligated to perform duties (like prayer), the performance of beneficial acts (like embracing Islam) is valid and accepted.

Key Terms
الأهلية (al-ahlīyah): The state of a person being such that a ruling can be validly attached to them.
القاصرة (al-qāsirah): Deficient capacity, resulting from deficiency in intellect or body.
حسن محض (husn mahd): An act whose goodness is undeniable in all circumstances, like faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the performance of faith (īmān) by a rational child?
A) It is invalid because the child is not obligated.
B) It is valid but not obligatory.
C) It is obligatory.
D) It is prohibited until puberty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, legal capacity determines obligation; a child with deficient capacity can validly perform beneficial acts, but they are not obligatory.

The Child's Obligation for Faith: Original vs. Performance Obligation
Analysing the evidence that a child is not obligated to perform iman immediately

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between original obligation (wujub al-asl) and performance obligation (wujub al-ada') in the Hanafi legal theory, and apply that distinction to the case of a child's obligation for iman.

Core Idea
A discerning child is obligated for iman in principle, but performance is deferred – a key Hanafi distinction.

In this passage, the author argues that a child with sound reasoning (sabi mumayyiz) is indeed obligated for faith (iman) at the level of original obligation, but the actual performance is not demanded immediately due to the child's incomplete capacity. This distinction between wujub al-asl and wujub al-ada' is central to the Hanafi theory of taklif. The discussion also addresses a potential counter-example from marriage annulment and refutes the view that the child has no obligation at all.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
The author states that the child is mukallaf bil-iman, but only if his discernment (tamyiz) is sufficient. Note that not every child is obligated; it requires the ability to reason soundly.
This is the starting point of the analysis.
2
Distinguish between wujub al-asl and wujub al-ada'
Original obligation (wujub al-asl) is the ruling that an act is required in principle, while performance obligation (wujub al-ada') is the immediate demand to fulfill it. The author separates these for the child.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the marriage example
The passage uses a girl who has not menstruated: if she is not described as a believer, her marriage remains valid due to doubt about her discernment. But if she is described as a disbeliever, the marriage is annulled because she is considered a capable obstinate disbeliever.
This shows that the child's disbelief has worldly consequences, indicating she is mukallaf in principle.
4
Refute the opposing view
Some argue that if obligations were originally binding, the child's performing the act would be performing an obligation, which is false. The author responds that the concession here is one of nullification (rukhsat isqat), meaning the obligation is abrogated, so performing it is not performing an obligation.
The author also notes that unlike the traveler's rukhsa (which involves sin if performed), the child's act of iman carries no sin.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The child's original obligation for iman stands, but the obligation to perform is deferred until full capacity is reached. Therefore, the child is rewarded for iman and faces worldly consequences for kufr.
This is the mutabbi' (operative) view in the Hanafi school.

المقالة الثانية في الأحكام أيضاً، والذي يظهر لهذا العبد أن الصبي مكلف بالإيمان، لكن لا كل صبي، بل صبي بلغ تمييزه إلى حد النظر الصحيح، وهذا الحد غير مضبوط كما سبق فالمراهقة لا يفسد نكاحها عند عدم الوصف بالإيمان للشبهة في البلوغ إلى حد التمييز وبالشبهة لا يرتفع النكاح القائم بيقين. وأما حالها في الآخرة فموكول إلى الله، فإن بلغت في علمه حد التكليف يعذبها وإلاّ لا، وأما عند الوصف بالكفر فقد علم أنها صلحت للنظر لكن كابرت العقل حيث أتت بالكفر فعلم كونها مكلفة كافرة، فحكم بانفساخ النكاح ، فليس في هذا دليل على أن الصبي غير مكلف بالإيمان عند أئمتنا أصلاً فتدبر (أقول : وفيه أنه لا يدل على نفي أصل الوجوب) للإيمان عن العاقلة والجواب أنه لم يقصد الدلالة عليه بل على نفي وجوب الأداء فأما نفس الوجوب فإن كان فلا يضرنا ولنا على القاضي خاصة أنه لو كان كل من الحقوق الإلهية (واجباً عليه، ثم سقط الوجوب دفعاً للحرج كما هو مذهبه (لكان) الصبي (الآتي) به (مؤدياً للواجب) لأنه صار مرخصاً في لزوم الأداء بعذر (كالمسافر إذا صام، واللازم هو كونه مؤدياً للواجب (باطل اتفاقاً فإن قيل : يجوز أن يكون رخصة إسقاط فلا يكون الآتي بها مؤدياً للواجب، قلت: إذا كان رخصة إسقاط فهي غير واجبة عليه بل وجوبه منسوخ ونحن لا ننكره، كما نقلنا البيهقي، وإنما النزاع في أن الوجوب ثابت عليه أم لا وأيضاً قال في الجواب (وليس رخصة إسقاط لعدم الإثم بالاتفاق في الإتيان وفيها يأثم في الإتيان كصلاة المسافر إذا أتمها فتدبر.
The second article on rulings also. The apparent view to this servant is that the child is obligated with faith, but not every child; rather a child whose discernment has reached the level of correct consideration. This limit is not defined as previously. So a girl who has not yet menstruated does not have her marriage invalidated when she is not described with faith due to the doubt about her attaining the limit of discernment, and by doubt the marriage established with certainty is not removed. As for her state in the afterlife, it is left to Allah; if in His knowledge she has reached the limit of obligation, He will punish her, otherwise not. As for when she is described with disbelief, it is known that she is fit for consideration but she fought the intellect by committing disbelief, so it is known that she is a obligated disbeliever, therefore the marriage is ruled to be annulled. So in this there is no proof that the child is not obligated with faith according to our imams at all. So reflect. (I say: And in it there is no proof for negating the original obligation of faith from the responsible person. The answer is that it was not intended to indicate that, but rather to negate the obligation of performance. As for the obligation itself, if it exists, it does not harm us. And we have a specific argument against the judge: if every divine right were obligatory upon him and then the obligation fell as a concession to remove hardship, as is his doctrine, then the child performing it would be performing an obligation because he became licensed in the necessity of performance due to an excuse, like the traveler when he fasts. The necessary consequence is that he is performing an obligation, which is false by consensus. If it is said: It is possible that it is a concession of nullification, so the one performing it is not performing an obligation. I say: If it is a concession of nullification, then it is not obligatory upon him; rather its obligation is abrogated, and we do not deny that, as we narrated from al-Bayhaqi. The dispute is only whether the obligation is established upon him or not. Also, he said in the answer: It is not a concession of nullification because there is no sin by consensus in performing it, and in [the opposite case] one is sinful in performing it, like the traveler when he completes his prayer. So reflect.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the taklif (obligation) of a child with respect to iman (faith). The author begins by stating his view that a child is mukallaf (obligated) with iman, but only if his discernment (tamyiz) has reached the level of sound reasoning. He then addresses a potential counter-example: a girl who has not reached puberty whose marriage is not invalidated if she is not described as a believer, due to doubt about her discernment. However, if she is described as a disbeliever, the marriage is annulled because her disbelief shows she is a capable and obstinate disbeliever. The author argues that this does not prove that a child is not obligated for iman at all. Then, in the marginal comment (أقول), the author responds to an objection: the earlier example only negates the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'), not the original obligation (asl al-wujub). He then refutes the view of a judge (al-Qadi) who might claim that if obligations are lifted as a concession, then the child performing the act would be performing an obligation, which leads to a contradiction. The author explains that the concession here is one of nullification (rukhsat isqat), meaning the obligation is abrogated, so performing it is not performing an obligation. The dispute is whether the obligation is originally established on the child or not. The author concludes that the concession is not one of nullification because there is no sin in performance, unlike the case of a traveler who completes his prayer (which would be sinful). Thus, the child's obligation of iman is confirmed in principle.

Key Terms
صبي (ṣabī): A child who has reached the age of discernment (tamyiz) but not puberty.
تمييز (tamyīz): The ability to understand and distinguish between beneficial and harmful matters.
تكليف (taklīf): Legal obligation that applies to a person with full capacity (reason and maturity).
أداء (adā’): The actual performance of an obligation.
رخصة (rukhṣa): A concession that eases or removes an obligation due to a valid excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the status of a discerning child (sabi mumayyiz) regarding the obligation of faith (iman)?
A) The child is not obligated at all until puberty.
B) The child has an original obligation (wujub al-asl) but not an immediate obligation of performance (wujub al-ada').
C) The child is fully obligated to perform all Islamic duties immediately.
D) The child's acts of faith are void because he lacks capacity.

Key Takeaway
A discerning child has an original obligation for iman (wujub al-asl) but the obligation to perform (wujub al-ada') is not immediate; this distinction is fundamental to the Hanafi theory of taklif.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
Legal Capacity, Faith, and Disbelief: The Child's Acts in Hanafi Usul
Defining legal capacity and applying its categories to child's iman and kufr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define legal capacity, distinguish its categories, classify acts by moral nature and legal right, and evaluate the Hanafi ruling on a child's disbelief using istihsan.

Core Idea
A child's disbelief is valid for worldly rulings by istihsan, even though it is pure harm and qiyas would invalidate it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut explains the foundational usul concept of legal capacity (ahliyyah) and then applies it to the acts of a discerning child. The author first defines capacity and its two types: complete (obligation of performance) and deficient (validity without obligation). He then classifies acts into rights of Allah and rights of servants, each subdivided into purely good, purely evil, and intermediate. The crux of the passage is the application to a child's iman (purely good, valid universally) and kufr (purely evil, valid for worldly rulings only by Hanafi istihsan, overriding qiyas). This reveals how Hanafi usul balances textual analogy with juristic preference to achieve coherent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Define legal capacity and its two types
Read the opening definition: ahliyyah is the quality that makes a person suitable for ruling attachment. Complete capacity (sound reason + physical maturity) imposes obligation; deficient capacity (lack of one) makes acts valid but not obligatory.
The child with tamyiz has deficient capacity due to bodily immaturity.
2
Classify acts into rights of Allah and rights of servants
Identify the two overarching categories (haqq Allah and haqq al-`abd), each with three subcategories: purely good/beneficial, purely evil/harmful, and intermediate. Relate these to the examples given: iman (purely good), kufr (purely evil), prayer (intermediate).
Rights of Allah consider the Lawgiver's command; rights of servants consider human interest.
3
Analyze the ruling on the child's iman
The author states iman is valid from a child by both qiyas and istihsan. Understand the reasoning: iman is purely beneficial, and the child is a subject of mercy, so it is valid. Anticipate and evaluate the objections about incidental harms (inheritance, marriage).
The harm is attributed to the disbelief of relatives, not to the child's own faith.
4
Analyze the dispute on the child's kufr
By qiyas, kufr should not be valid because it is pure harm (Shafi'i & Abu Yusuf). But the Hanafi school adopts istihsan: kufr is absolutely evil and makes the child wretched, so the excuse of childhood does not prevent worldly effects. Trace the thamarah al-khilaf: annulment of marriage and loss of inheritance.
Abu Yusuf agrees with the Imam on iman but with al-Shafi'i on kufr, showing internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Understand why the child is not killed for apostasy
Even though the child's disbelief is valid, killing is not applied because (1) the punishment for apostasy is for hiraba (warfare), which a child cannot commit; (2) the hadith forbids killing children; (3) there is a shubha (doubt) due to scholarly disagreement on the validity of the child's Islam, and hadd penalties are repelled by doubt.
The shubha here is about the cause (sabab), not the ruling, which some scholars contest.

عدا الأوقات المكروهة
Issue about capacity: (Legal capacity) is that a person is such that the ruling can attach to him. Complete capacity is with completeness of reason and body, i.e., being sane and adult, so the obligation of performance is incumbent. Deficient capacity is with deficiency in one of them, like the sane child (his body is deficient) or the insane adult (due to deficiency of reason). With deficient capacity, the validity of performance is established, not its obligation, as has passed. The detail regarding the child (and the insane is analogous) is that what accompanies deficient capacity is either a right of Allah (which considers the aspect of the Law) and it is three: purely good (whose goodness can never lapse), purely evil (whose evil can never lapse), and intermediate (which may be good or evil). Or it is a right of the servant (which considers the interests of the servant in its legislation) and it also is three: purely beneficial in this world, purely harmful in it, and intermediate (which may benefit or harm). The first (purely good) is like faith (iman), for it is purely good, its goodness never lapses, and it is purely beneficial because it is the source of happiness in both worlds. As for otherworldly happiness, it is apparent. As for worldly happiness, because by faith one becomes inviolable in blood and property and honored among people. Since it is purely beneficial, it is valid from the child by qiyas and istihsan, because he is a subject of mercy, so what is beneficial for him is valid. If it is said: Perhaps the Law did not consider it and made it like no faith? He said: The legal interdiction from the Lawgiver has not occurred, nor is it appropriate. For the Wise One cannot appropriately place an interdiction on what is the basis of happiness in both worlds. If you say: There is also harm in it, such as deprivation of inheritance when the testator is a disbeliever, and dissolution of marriage when the wife is a disbeliever. He answered: The harm of deprivation of inheritance and dissolution of marriage is not based on faith, but on the disbelief of the relative and wife. Their disbelief together with his faith causes religious antagonism, which necessitates that. The well-known maxim that an event is attributed to the nearest cause is not general, but only when the nearest cause is suitable. Here, faith is not suitable for attribution of harms, so the separation is not attributed to it. Even if it were granted that each of these harms occurred from his faith, it is incidental. As per essence, there is eternal happiness in it. How many things are established incidentally and not intended, like the child accepting a gift from a relative which results in emancipation, yet the child does not have the capacity to intend emancipation. Even if it were granted that it is essential, a slight harm is borne for much benefit. Another answer: We deny that this is a harm. For severing the bond between the fortunate and the unfortunate, which causes deprivation of inheritance, is great good. Likewise severing intimacy between them. So reflect. The second (purely evil) is like disbelief. By qiyas it is not valid because it is pure harm, and the child is a subject of mercy. This is the view of al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf. So Abu Yusuf agrees with the Imam in validating faith, and agrees with al-Shafi'i in not validating the child's disbelief. However, by istihsan in our school, his disbelief is valid. This difference is only regarding the rulings of this world. In the rulings of the afterlife, it is valid by consensus, so that if a disbelieving child dies, funeral prayer is not performed for him by consensus. The well-known interpretation of afterlife rulings is punishment in the Hereafter. This is an amazing thing: mercy in punishing for an infinite period while not permitting separation or deprivation of inheritance. Also, theological works are full of differences regarding the punishment of young disbelievers. They attribute to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) hesitation, and to the Ash'aris pardon based on His saying (interpretation of meaning): "And We never punish until We send a Messenger" [al-Isra': 15]. This contradicts the claimed consensus, unless the child is a non-rational disbeliever by following his mother. This is not far-fetched in the Imam's view because there is no excuse for anyone in ignorance of the Creator. But the Ash'ari argument refutes this. It is narrated with a good chain from Abu Hurayra that Allah will test them with fire and command them to enter it: whoever obeys finds it cool and is pardoned, whoever disobeys is punished. So there is no consensus either. Perhaps he meant the agreement of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i with them. (The face of istihsan is that disbelief is absolutely prohibited, always evil, and he has committed it making him wretched, so it is not dropped by an unacceptable excuse. The excuse of being a subject of mercy due to childhood is not acceptable because this complete wretchedness removes him from being a subject of mercy, for mercy does not make the perfectly wretched happy. If his disbelief is valid and his wretchedness is considered, then his believing wife becomes separated from him, and inheritance is prohibited due to apostasy. If you say: Why is he not killed for apostasy? He replied: He is not killed because killing the apostate is not merely due to apostasy, but due to waging war (hiraba), and he is not capable of that. The prohibition of killing children has been reported in authentic narrations in the Sahihs. If you say: Why is he not killed after reaching adulthood? He replied: He is not killed after adulthood either, because there is a difference of opinion among scholars regarding the validity of his Islam. Some say his Islam is valid, so his disbelief is apostasy, while others say his Islam is not valid, so his disbelief is not apostasy. So the difference creates a doubt (shubha) regarding the establishment of apostasy, and the prescribed punishment is repelled by doubt. That is what they said. But there is a point: The doubt that repels the punishment is the doubt arising in the establishment of the cause itself, not the doubt about whether it is a cause. Otherwise, a hadd punishment would not be established by a disputed cause nor by a khabar al-wahid. Here, the cause is established without any rejection, so repelling it is not sound. Contemplate. If they considered the repelling once as a doubt about its return, that would have some face and suffice. So reflect. The third (intermediate) is like prayer and similar bodily acts of worship, which are prescribed at times and outside disliked times.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage defines legal capacity (ahliyyah) and its two types: complete capacity (with sound mind and body, i.e., major and sane) which entails obligation of performance; and deficient capacity (when one of the two is lacking, e.g., a child with sound mind but deficient body, or an insane adult with deficient mind) which makes acts valid but not obligatory. The author then classifies acts into two categories: rights of Allah (based on Sharī'a proper) and rights of servants (based on human interests). Each is subdivided into three: purely good, purely evil, and intermediate. The example of purely good is iman (faith). Iman is purely beneficial and good, so it is valid from a child by both qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (equity). The child is a subject of mercy, so what benefits him is valid. Objections about harms (like loss of inheritance or annulment of marriage) are answered: these harms are incidental and not due to faith itself; they are due to the disbelief of relatives. Faith in itself is purely beneficial. The second category is purely evil, like kufr (disbelief). By qiyas, a child's kufr should not be valid because it is pure harm and the child is a subject of mercy. This is the view of al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf. However, by Hanafi istihsan, the child's kufr is valid for worldly rulings (e.g., an apostate child's marriage is annulled, and he loses inheritance). In afterlife matters, there is consensus that a disbelieving child will be punished (according to most), though there is some debate. The author then discusses why such a child is not killed for apostasy: because killing is for hiraba (warfare), children are exempt by hadith, and there is a doubt (shubha) about the validity of his Islam due to scholarly disagreement, which repels the hadd penalty. The third category is intermediate acts like prayer, which are valid from a child but may be disliked at certain times (like at sunrise).

Key Terms
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity: the quality in a person that makes him suitable for the attachment of rulings.
أهلية كاملة (ahliyyah kāmilah): Complete capacity: being an adult and sane, which necessitates obligation of performance.
أهلية قاصرة (ahliyyah qāṣirah): Deficient capacity: lacking either reason or bodily maturity, resulting in validity of performance without obligation.
حق الله (ḥaqq Allāh): A category of right where the primary consideration is the command of the Lawgiver, not individual interest.
حق العبد (ḥaqq al-‘abd): A category of right where the legislation considers the benefit of the servant.
حسن محض (ḥasan maḥḍ): Purely good: an act whose goodness never lapses under any circumstance.
قبيح محض (qabīḥ maḥḍ): Purely evil: an act whose evil never lapses under any circumstance.
دائر بين الحسن والقبيح (dā'ir bayna al-ḥusn wa al-qubḥ): Intermediate: an act that may be good or evil depending on context.
استحسان (istiḥsān): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas (analogy) in certain cases to achieve a more just or appropriate ruling.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a hadd (fixed) punishment.
حرابة (ḥirāba): Waging war or armed rebellion, which is the actual basis for the capital punishment often associated with apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary reason that the child's kufr is valid for worldly rulings, overriding the qiyas argument?
A) The child is an adult in Shari'ah because of tamyiz.
B) The absolute evil of kufr and the child's wretchedness remove him from being a subject of mercy.
C) The child's parents consented to his disbelief.
D) The child is capable of intentional acts and must face consequences.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul framework defines legal capacity, classifies acts by their moral nature, and employs istihsan to validate even harmful acts from a child when the absolute evil of the act overrides the excuse of childhood.

Purely Beneficial Acts of a Minor: Definition and Ruling
Definition and ruling on purely beneficial acts of a minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-nāfiʿ al-maḥḍ, apply the Hanafi rule that such acts are valid without guardian permission, and distinguish the rulings for a free minor and a slave minor.

Core Idea
Pure benefit removes the need for guardian oversight — a minor's acceptance of a gift is valid without permission.

In Hanafi usul, the capacity of a minor to perform legal acts depends on whether the act carries potential harm. This lesson explores the fourth category: purely beneficial acts. Understanding this category is essential for determining when a minor can act independently and when a guardian is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitional structure
Note that the author defines 'al-nāfiʿ al-maḥḍ' (pure benefit) by example and then states its ruling: valid without guardian permission. The key operative phrase is 'لأنه نفع محض' (because it is pure benefit).
The definition is functional—it is defined by its legal effect, not by a lexical definition.
2
Extract the general principle
The text explains that the guardian is only needed to prevent harm from potential losses. Since pure benefit has no harm, the minor may act alone. Formulate this as a qāʿida: 'What is purely beneficial does not require guardian permission.'
This principle is based on the logic of guardian's role, not on a specific textual proof.
3
Apply to the first example: accepting a gift
The text gives 'accepting a gift' as a clear instance. Rule: the minor may accept directly, and the gift is valid (sahih).
4
Apply to the second example: hiring oneself out
A free minor's contract to hire himself is void ab initio due to potential hardship, but if he completes the work, the benefit materializes, so wages become due. For a slave minor, wages are only due if the work is completed safely; if the hired property perishes, only value (as usurpation) is due.
This shows that pure benefit can emerge after performance, even if the initial contract was invalid.
5
Apply to the third example: radkh (spoils)
A minor may not fight due to danger, but receiving a share of spoils is pure benefit, so he may receive it without guardian permission. This is by consensus.
The principle of pure benefit overrides the prohibition of fighting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والرابع) وهو حق العبد النافع المحض (كقبول الهبة يصح مباشرته منه بلا إذن وليه لأنه نفع محض والولي إنما جعل ولياً لئلا يستضر بالغرامات فتخص الحاجة إليه فيما يحتمل المضرة وأما ما هو نافع محض فلا يحتاج فيه إليه فيصح من غير إذنه (ولذلك) أي لأجل أن النافع في حق الصبي يثبت من غير إذن الولي تجب أجرة الصبي المحجور) إذا استأجر نفسه وفرغ من العمل مع بطلان العقد الذي عقده (إذا كان) الصبي (حراً) لأن بطلان عقده إنما كان لاحتمال أن تضره المشقة، فإذا فرغ من العمل بقي النفع الذي كان في العقد فلا وجه لبطلان العقد في هذا، فوجب الأجر المسمى دون أجر المثل (وأما العبد) المحجور إذا أجر نفسه فيجب له الأجر بشرط السلامة بعد الفراغ من العمل لما بينا (فلو هلك) هذه في الإجارة ( فالقيمة واجبة (لا) الأجر لأن المستأجر يصير غاصباً بالاستخدام من غير إذن السيد، فإذا هلك وجب القيمة عليه وملك العبد بالضمان، فظهر أنه استخدم ملك نفسه، فلا أجر (و) لذا (استحق) الصبي (الرضخ بالخاء المعجمة وهو مال أقل من السهم من الغنيمة (مع عدم جواز شهود القتل أي القتال (بدون الإذن بالإجماع لأن عدم جواز الشهود إنما كان لدفع احتمال ضرر الموت والجرح مع عدم الوجوب عليه وأما حال أخذ الغنيمة فنفع محض
(The fourth) is the right of the servant which is purely beneficial (like accepting a gift). He may perform it directly without his guardian's permission because it is pure benefit. The guardian is only appointed to prevent harm from penalties, so the need for him is restricted to matters that may involve harm. As for what is purely beneficial, there is no need for him, so it is valid without his permission. (Therefore) because benefit for the minor is established without the guardian's permission, the wages of a minor under interdiction become obligatory if he hires himself and completes the work, despite the invalidity of the contract he made, provided he is free. The invalidity of his contract was only due to the possibility of hardship, so once he completed the work, the benefit that was in the contract remains, so the contract is not invalidated, and the named wages are due, not the fair wage. As for a slave under interdiction who hires himself: wages are due to him with the condition of safety after completion of the work. If the hired object perishes, then the value is due, not the wages, because the employer becomes a usurper by employing without the master's permission; thus if it perishes, the value is due and the slave owns the value by virtue of liability. So it appears he used his own property, so no wages. Hence the minor deserves the radkh (a minor portion of the spoils) even though he may not attend battle without permission by consensus, because prohibition of attendance was only to repel potential harm of death and injury while it is not obligatory upon him. As for taking the spoils, it is pure benefit.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth category of actions for a minor: those that are purely beneficial. The author explains that such actions—like accepting a gift—are valid without guardian permission because the guardian's role is to prevent harm, not block pure gain. The ruling extends to earning wages: if a minor completes hired work, even if the original contract was void (due to incapacity), the minor deserves the agreed wage because benefit has materialized. For a slave minor, wages are due only if the work is completed safely; if the hired object perishes, the employer pays its value (as a usurper), not wages. Similarly, a minor may receive a small share of war spoils (radkh) even though he may not fight, because receiving property is pure benefit. The key principle is that any act yielding pure benefit for the minor is enforceable without guardian oversight, as there is no risk of harm to him.

Key Terms
النافع المحض (al-nāfiʿ al-maḥḍ): An action that yields benefit without any potential harm to the minor.
الرضخ (al-radhkh): A portion of spoils less than a full share, given to those who did not fight but participated in auxiliary roles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does a free minor who hires himself out receive wages despite the contract being void?
A) If the guardian ratifies the contract
B) If he completes the work
C) If the employer is a Muslim
D) If he is a slave

Key Takeaway
A minor may independently perform any act that is purely beneficial, and even initially void contracts become effective if they result in realized benefit without harm.

Purely Harmful Acts for Minors: Ownership vs. Execution
Usul definition of purely harmful acts with a dispute on minor's divorce and an exception for judge lending.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between ownership and execution of the power of divorce to determine the validity of a minor's purely harmful act, and explain why a judge may lend a minor's property as preservation.

Core Idea
A minor owns the power of divorce but may only execute it when needed; judge's lending is preservation, not donation.

This lesson explores the fifth category of actions that a minor cannot perform: purely harmful acts. The text clarifies a common misconception: while a minor cannot execute a harmful act like divorce unnecessarily, he still possesses the power to do so as an inherent right of marriage. It then addresses an apparent exception—a judge lending a minor's property—which is classified as preservation rather than donation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that purely harmful acts (al-ḍār al-maḥḍ) are those with no benefit and only harm to the minor. The text uses divorce as an example.
2
Analyze the dispute
Some earlier Hanafi scholars claimed the minor's wife is not a valid subject for divorce at all. Al-Sarakhsi refutes this, arguing that the power of divorce is a necessary consequence of marriage ownership.
Distinguish between owning the power (milk al-ṭalāq) and executing it (īqāʿ).
3
Apply the distinction
If executing divorce is harmful, the minor cannot do it unnecessarily. But if needed to repel harm from the wife, it becomes valid. This shows the criterion is harm, not absolute incapacity.
The harm is in the execution, not in the ownership.
4
Examine the judge lending exception
The judge lending a minor's property to a solvent person is classified as preservation because the debt is enforceable. Thus it is not a purely harmful donation. The text notes that due to corruption, this ruling is not followed today.
Contrast with father who cannot lend because risk of denial exists.
5
Synthesize the principle
The general rule: a minor cannot perform a purely harmful act. But where harm can be repelled or avoided (like lending for preservation), the act is permitted. The key is the legal characterization of the act.
This demonstrates the usul principle of considering the cause (sabab) and effect (athar) in legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والخامس) وهو الضار المحض كالطلاق) ونحوه، فلا يملكه ولو بإذن وليه، كما لا يملكه عليه أي على الصبي (غيره) فعلى هذا امرأته ليست محلاً للطلاق، قالوا : لأنه لما كان ضاراً بالقطع، وقد كان ولاية الولي ليندفع الضرر بانضمام رأيه ولا اندفاع ها هنا بطل الولاية في هذا القسم بالكلية فتأمل فيه (قال) الإمام شمس (الأئمة السرخسي : (زعم بعض مشايخنا أن هذا الحكم أي حكم الطلاق غير مشروع أصلاً، حتى أن امرأته لا تكون محلاً للطلاق) بل صارت في هذا الحكم الحكم كالأجنبية وهذا وهم فإن الطلاق يملك بملك النكاح) فهو من لوازمه فلا ينفك النكاح عن ملك الطلاق ولا ضرر فيه أي في ملك الطلاق حتى لا يملك الصبي، بل في عدم الملك ضرر (وإنما هو في الإيقاع) فإنه يبطل به ملك النكاح فلا يصلح للإيقاع لكن ربما ينشأ من الزوجة مضرات عظيمة، فحينئذ لا ضرر في الإيقاع (فلو تحققت الحاجة إليه لدفع الضرر كان صحيحاً هذا أشبه بالصواب والله أعلم بأحكامه. فإن قلت: فإذا كان لا يملك ما فيه مضرة أصلاً فلم يملك القاضي إقراض ماله من المليء، فإنه متبرع لا نفع فيه أصلاً؟ قال : (وإنما يجوز إقراض القاضي ماله من المليء لا لأنه تبرع، بل (لأنه حفظ) له، لأنه في يد ضمين، فلا احتمال للهلاك مع قدرة الاقتضاء بعلمه فلا احتمال للجحود، وها هنا بحث : فإن احتمال الجحود وإن انسد لكنها هنا احتمالات أخرى، كانعزال القاضي أو إفلاس المديون أو غيبوبة منقطعة أو غير ذلك، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية الربانية : لا يؤخذ بهذه الرواية لظهور الخيانة اليوم في القضاء فافهم بخلاف الأب فإنه لا يملك إقراض مال ابنه الصغير (إلا في رواية وجهها أنه نوع من الحفظ لأنه يصير في يد ضمين قادر على الأداء، وجه الأولى أنه يحتمل الهلاك بالجحود ، بخلاف القاضي فإن علمه ملزم فلا يضر الجحود
(The fifth) is purely harmful actions like divorce and the like. The minor does not have the power to do it even with his guardian's permission, just as no one else can do it on his behalf. Thus his wife is not a valid subject for divorce. They said: Since it is definitely harmful, and the guardian's authority was given to repel harm by combining his opinion, and here harm is not repelled, authority in this category is entirely nullified. Consider this. Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: Some of our scholars claimed that this ruling—that divorce is entirely unlegislated—so much so that his wife is not a valid subject for divorce, but becomes like a stranger. This is a delusion. For the power to divorce is owned by virtue of possessing the marriage contract; it is a necessary consequence, so marriage cannot be separated from the power to divorce. There is no harm in owning the power of divorce, such that the minor would not own it; rather, not owning it is harmful. The harm is only in its execution, for it invalidates the ownership of the marriage contract, so he is not fit to execute it. But sometimes great harms may arise from the wife, and in that case there is no harm in execution. So if the need to repel harm is realized, it is valid; this is more correct, and Allah knows best. If you ask: Since he does not own anything harmful, then why does the judge have the power to lend his [the minor's] property to a wealthy person, for this is a donation with no benefit? He said: The judge is allowed to lend his property to a wealthy person not because it is a donation, but because it is preservation; for it is in the hand of a guarantor, so there is no risk of loss given the ability to reclaim through his knowledge, and no risk of denial. There is a discussion here: Although the risk of denial is blocked, other risks exist, such as the judge being removed, the debtor's bankruptcy, prolonged absence, etc. The author of 'Mintala' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya al-Rabbaniyya' said: This narration should not be acted upon due to the prevalence of treachery in judiciary today. So understand. Unlike the father, who cannot lend his minor son's property except in one narration that considers it a form of preservation because it becomes in the hand of a capable guarantor. The primary view is that it risks loss due to denial, unlike the judge whose knowledge is binding so denial does not harm.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses the fifth category: purely harmful actions. The text first states that a minor cannot perform a purely harmful act like divorce, even with guardian permission, because the guardian's role is to prevent harm. Imam Sarakhsi corrects a misconception: some scholars thought a minor's wife is not a valid subject for divorce, but Sarakhsi explains that owning the power to divorce is inherent in marriage, so the minor possesses it. The harm lies in executing the divorce unnecessarily, but if there is genuine need (e.g., harm from the wife), the divorce is valid. The passage then answers an objection: if a minor cannot do harmful acts, how can a judge lend the minor's property—a donation with no apparent benefit? The response distinguishes: lending to a solvent person is preservation, not a donation, because the money is in safe hands. However, due to corruption in judiciary, this narration is not followed. The father cannot lend the minor's property, as the risk of denial exists unlike with the judge whose knowledge prevents denial.

Key Terms
الضار المحض (al-ḍār al-maḥḍ): An action that brings only harm to the minor with no benefit.
إقراض القاضي (iqrāḍ al-qāḍī): The act of a judge lending a minor's property to a trustworthy person for preservation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the judge is the guardian
B) Because the borrower is solvent and the judge can enforce repayment
C) Because it earns profit
D) Because the minor is not harmed

Key Takeaway
A minor owns the power of divorce as a consequence of marriage but can only execute it to repel harm; a judge's lending of the minor's property is preservation, not a donation, but is restricted in practice.
